## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate (dP_dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P), a core problem in population ecology. The relationships are typically governed by ordinary differential equations incorporating density dependence, Allee effects, environmental fluctuations, and allometric scaling.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth with constant per-capita rate)
- Logistic (Verhulst) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (density-dependent self-limitation, carrying capacity)
- Generalized logistic (theta-logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**(c2 + 1) (flexible density-dependence curvature)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (asymmetric sigmoid growth with shape parameter c2)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (decelerating growth, common in tumor and population aging models)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (allometric growth where anabolic and catabolic terms scale differently)
- Allee effect (cubic model): dP_dt = c0 * P**3 + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P (positive density dependence at low population, unstable zero equilibrium)
- Logistic with linear time-varying growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P - c2 * P**2 (secular environmental trend)
- Logistic with exponential time dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (carrying capacity changing exponentially over time)
- Logistic with sinusoidal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (seasonal resource fluctuations)
- Logistic with saturable harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P / (c3 + P) (Type II functional response predation or harvesting)
- Logistic with periodic growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P - c3 * P**2 (seasonally varying intrinsic growth rate)
- Polynomial with immigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P - c2 * P**2 (constant immigration or stocking)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (density-independent allometric scaling when c1 ŌēĀ 1)
- Multiplicative time-density interaction: dP_dt = c0 * P * t * (c1 - P) (time-limited growth window)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate (dP/dt)/P is a function of P alone, indicating density-dependent regulation.
- Negative quadratic or higher-order polynomial terms in P imply self-limitation and the existence of a carrying capacity.
- Appearance of P * log(P) signals Gompertz-like growth with a steady decline in relative growth rate.
- Rational terms of the form P/(c+P) in the growth equation indicate saturable predation or harvesting (Type II functional response).
- Cubic or higher odd-degree polynomial in dP/dt suggests Allee effects, where population growth is negative at very low densities.
- Explicit time dependence (t) in growth coefficients represents non-autonomous dynamics driven by environmental change or seasonality.
- Sinusoidal terms indicate periodic external forcing, such as seasonal resource pulses or temperature cycles.
- Power-law terms P^a with a ŌēĀ 1 reflect allometric scaling, often from size-dependent metabolic rates.
- Constant additive terms not multiplied by P suggest immigration, stocking, or constant removal processes.
- Combined polynomial and rational structures enable modelling of intrinsic growth alongside saturating biotic interactions.
